### [1] [Granulon: Awakening Pixel-Level Visual Encoders with Adaptive Multi-Granularity Semantics for MLLM](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08800)
*Junyuan Mao,Qiankun Li,Linghao Meng,Zhicheng He,Xinliang Zhou,Kun Wang,Yang Liu,Yueming Jin*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Granulon is a DINOv3-based multimodal LLM that adaptively controls visual granularity using a text-conditioned controller and token aggregation, enabling pixel-to-fine-to-coarse reasoning in one pass and yielding ~30% accuracy gains with ~20% less hallucination over strong baselines.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: CLIP-style encoders excel at global semantic alignment but miss fine details; DINOv3 offers strong pixel-level perception but weak high-level abstraction. MLLMs need multi-granularity visual reasoning, which neither approach alone provides.

Method: Introduce (1) a text-conditioned Granularity Controller that adjusts the abstraction level based on the semantic scope of the input text; (2) an Adaptive Token Aggregation module that performs granularity-guided pooling and relation-aware clustering to compress features into compact, semantically rich visual tokens; together enabling unified pixel→fine→coarse reasoning within a single forward pass.

Result: Across extensive experiments, Granulon reportedly improves accuracy by about 30% and reduces hallucinations by about 20%, outperforming models using alternative visual encoders under identical setups; analyses are said to be interpretable.

Conclusion: Adaptive, text-guided control of visual abstraction combined with token aggregation allows MLLMs to balance fine-grained perception with coarse semantics, improving accuracy and reliability over CLIP- or plain DINOv3-based encoders.

Abstract: Recent advances in multimodal large language models largely rely on CLIP-based visual encoders, which emphasize global semantic alignment but struggle with fine-grained visual understanding. In contrast, DINOv3 provides strong pixel-level perception yet lacks coarse-grained semantic abstraction, leading to limited multi-granularity reasoning. To address this gap, we propose Granulon, a novel DINOv3-based MLLM with adaptive granularity augmentation. Granulon introduces a text-conditioned granularity Controller that dynamically adjusts the visual abstraction level according to the semantic scope of the textual input, and an Adaptive Token Aggregation module that performs granularity-guided pooling and relation-aware clustering to produce compact, semantically rich visual tokens. This design enables unified "pixel-to-fine-to-coarse" reasoning within a single forward pass. Extensive and interpretable experiments demonstrate that Granulon improves accuracy by ~30% and reduces hallucination by ~20%, outperforming all visual encoders under identical settings.

</details>


### [2] [Where, What, Why: Toward Explainable 3D-GS Watermarking](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08809)
*Mingshu Cai,Jiajun Li,Osamu Yoshie,Yuya Ieiri,Yixuan Li*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A representation-native watermarking framework for 3D Gaussian Splatting that separates carrier selection from quality preservation, using expert priors, budget-aware allocation, and gradient-masked finetuning to embed view-consistent, robust, and imperceptible watermarks, outperforming prior work in PSNR (+0.83 dB) and bit accuracy (+1.24%).


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: As 3D Gaussian Splatting becomes standard for interactive 3D assets, there is a need for watermarks that survive rendering and common distortions while remaining invisible. Prior methods either are 2D-centric, not robust to perturbations, or degrade visual quality; a representation-native solution promises better robustness–quality trade-offs and auditable placement of watermark carriers.

Method: (1) Trio-Experts module operates on Gaussian primitives to derive priors that identify promising watermark carriers. (2) Safety and Budget Aware Gate (SBAG) assigns Gaussians either to carriers (optimized for bit resilience under perturbation and bitrate budgets) or to compensators (insulated from watermark loss to preserve visuals). (3) A channel-wise group mask controls gradient propagation during finetuning, limiting parameter updates, repairing local artifacts, and preserving high-frequency details without runtime overhead. (4) Decoupled finetuning yields per-Gaussian attributions for explainability (where/why bits are carried).

Result: Delivers view-consistent watermark persistence and robustness to common image distortions (compression, noise), with a favorable robustness–quality trade-off versus state of the art, showing +0.83 dB PSNR and +1.24% bit-accuracy improvements.

Conclusion: Separating carrier selection from quality preservation in a representation-native pipeline with budget-aware allocation and gradient-masked updates yields robust, imperceptible, and explainable watermarking for 3D Gaussian Splatting. The approach appears effective and auditable, though broader testing against stronger 3D/geometry attacks and detailed capacity/runtime analyses would strengthen claims.

Abstract: As 3D Gaussian Splatting becomes the de facto representation for interactive 3D assets, robust yet imperceptible watermarking is critical. We present a representation-native framework that separates where to write from how to preserve quality. A Trio-Experts module operates directly on Gaussian primitives to derive priors for carrier selection, while a Safety and Budget Aware Gate (SBAG) allocates Gaussians to watermark carriers, optimized for bit resilience under perturbation and bitrate budgets, and to visual compensators that are insulated from watermark loss. To maintain fidelity, we introduce a channel-wise group mask that controls gradient propagation for carriers and compensators, thereby limiting Gaussian parameter updates, repairing local artifacts, and preserving high-frequency details without increasing runtime. Our design yields view-consistent watermark persistence and strong robustness against common image distortions such as compression and noise, while achieving a favorable robustness-quality trade-off compared with prior methods. In addition, decoupled finetuning provides per-Gaussian attributions that reveal where the message is carried and why those carriers are selected, enabling auditable explainability. Compared with state-of-the-art methods, our approach achieves a PSNR improvement of +0.83 dB and a bit-accuracy gain of +1.24%.

</details>


### [3] [VisionCreator-R1: A Reflection-Enhanced Native Visual-Generation Agentic Model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08812)
*Jinxiang Lai,Wenzhe Zhao,Zexin Lu,Hualei Zhang,Qinyu Yang,Rongwei Quan,Zhimin Li,Shuai Shao,Song Guo,Qinglin Lu*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Introduces VisionCreator-R1, a visual generation agent with explicit reflection and a Reflection-Plan Co-Optimization (RPCO) training scheme that addresses RL credit-assignment issues; it outperforms Gemini2.5Pro on single- and multi-image benchmarks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current multi-image visual generation agents are mainly plan-driven and lack systematic reflection to detect and correct mid-trajectory visual errors. Standard RL struggles to learn reflection behaviors due to noisy credit assignment, motivating new training signals and curricula.

Method: Design a native visual generation agent with an explicit reflection module (VisionCreator-R1). Propose RPCO: (1) supervised pretraining on a self-built VCR-SFT dataset that segregates reflection-strong single-image trajectories and planning-strong multi-image trajectories; (2) RL co-optimization on a VCR-RL dataset. Through trajectory-level analysis, identify an optimization asymmetry: plan rewards reliably improve planning, but reflection learning is unstable under typical RL credit assignment, informing the training design.

Result: A unified VisionCreator-R1 agent achieves consistent SOTA-like gains over Gemini2.5Pro on public benchmarks and the new VCR-bench, covering both single-image and multi-image tasks.

Conclusion: Explicit reflection, coupled with RPCO and a tailored curriculum, overcomes RL’s reflection-learning instability and yields a broadly stronger visual generation agent. The work also contributes new datasets/benchmarks and demonstrates improved mid-trajectory error correction in practice.

Abstract: Visual content generation has advanced from single-image to multi-image workflows, yet existing agents remain largely plan-driven and lack systematic reflection mechanisms to correct mid-trajectory visual errors. To address this limitation, we propose VisionCreator-R1, a native visual generation agent with explicit reflection, together with a Reflection-Plan Co-Optimization (RPCO) training methodology. Through extensive experiments and trajectory-level analysis, we uncover reflection-plan optimization asymmetry in reinforcement learning (RL): planning can be reliably optimized via plan rewards, while reflection learning is hindered by noisy credit assignment. Guided by this insight, our RPCO first trains on the self-constructed VCR-SFT dataset with reflection-strong single-image trajectories and planning-strong multi-image trajectories, then co-optimization on VCR-RL dataset via RL. This yields our unified VisionCreator-R1 agent, which consistently outperforms Gemini2.5Pro on existing benchmarks and our VCR-bench covering single-image and multi-image tasks.

</details>


### [4] [Computer Vision-Based Vehicle Allotment System using Perspective Mapping](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08827)
*Prachi Nandi,Sonakshi Satapathy,Suchismita Chinara*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Proposes a low-cost, computer-vision smart parking system that fuses four camera views via inverse perspective mapping and uses YOLOv8 to detect vehicles and vacancies, then visualizes available spots in a 3D scene to guide users.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Urban congestion and sustainability goals demand more efficient parking management. Traditional fixed sensors suffer from accuracy limits and integration complexity, especially in dense cities, motivating a more adaptive, higher-accuracy allocation approach.

Method: Use object detection (YOLOv8) to recognize vehicles/empty spaces from four cameras; apply inverse perspective mapping (IPM) to fuse multi-view images into a top-down representation; derive vacancy data and render a simulated 3D parking environment with a 3D Cartesian plot for user guidance.

Result: Delivers a cost-effective, easy-to-implement prototype that extracts vacant-space information from fused multi-camera inputs and presents it in a 3D interface; the abstract claims improved adaptability over fixed sensors but reports no quantitative performance metrics.

Conclusion: Computer vision with multi-camera IPM offers a practical and scalable alternative to sensor-based smart parking, enabling dynamic assessment of parking layouts and guiding users to open spaces; further evaluation would solidify its comparative advantages.

Abstract: Smart city research envisions a future in which data-driven solutions and sustainable infrastructure work together to define urban living at the crossroads of urbanization and technology. Within this framework, smart parking systems play an important role in reducing urban congestion and supporting sustainable transportation. Automating parking solutions have considerable benefits, such as increased efficiency and less reliance on human involvement, but obstacles such as sensor limitations and integration complications remain. To overcome them, a more sophisticated car allotment system is required, particularly in heavily populated urban areas. Computer vision, with its higher accuracy and adaptability, outperforms traditional sensor-based systems for recognizing vehicles and vacant parking spaces. Unlike fixed sensor technologies, computer vision can dynamically assess a wide range of visual inputs while adjusting to changing parking layouts. This research presents a cost-effective, easy-to-implement smart parking system utilizing computer vision and object detection models like YOLOv8. Using inverse perspective mapping (IPM) to merge images from four camera views, we extract data on vacant spaces. The system simulates a 3D parking environment, representing available spots with a 3D Cartesian plot to guide users.

</details>


### [5] [A Lightweight Multi-Cancer Tumor Localization Framework for Deployable Digital Pathology](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08844)
*Brian Isett,Rebekah Dadey,Aofei Li,Ryan C. Augustin,Kate Smith,Aatur D. Singhi,Qiangqiang Gu,Riyue Bao*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: MuCTaL is a DenseNet169-based, multi-cancer tumor localizer trained on ~80k H&E tiles from four cancers; it attains high tile-level AUC on seen cancers (0.97) and moderate generalization to an unseen cancer (PDAC, 0.71), with a scalable heatmap inference pipeline and open-source release.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Single-cancer tumor detectors often lack robustness when applied across different tumor types. Robust, generalizable tumor localization from H&E WSIs is needed to enable spatial analysis, molecular profiling, and tissue architecture studies across cancers.

Method: Balanced multi-cancer training using transfer learning with DenseNet169 on 79,984 non-overlapping tiles from melanoma, hepatocellular carcinoma, colorectal cancer, and non-small cell lung cancer; development of a scalable inference workflow producing spatial tumor probability heatmaps compatible with digital pathology tools.

Result: Tile-level ROC-AUC = 0.97 on validation data from the four training cancers; ROC-AUC = 0.71 on an independent pancreatic ductal adenocarcinoma cohort; release of code and pretrained models.

Conclusion: Balanced multi-cancer training at modest scale can deliver strong in-domain tumor localization and partial out-of-domain generalization, while providing practical deployment through heatmap generation and open-source resources.

Abstract: Accurate localization of tumor regions from hematoxylin and eosin-stained whole-slide images is fundamental for translational research including spatial analysis, molecular profiling, and tissue architecture investigation. However, deep learning-based tumor detection trained within specific cancers may exhibit reduced robustness when applied across different tumor types. We investigated whether balanced training across cancers at modest scale can achieve high performance and generalize to unseen tumor types. A multi-cancer tumor localization model (MuCTaL) was trained on 79,984 non-overlapping tiles from four cancers (melanoma, hepatocellular carcinoma, colorectal cancer, and non-small cell lung cancer) using transfer learning with DenseNet169. The model achieved a tile-level ROC-AUC of 0.97 in validation data from the four training cancers, and 0.71 on an independent pancreatic ductal adenocarcinoma cohort. A scalable inference workflow was built to generate spatial tumor probability heatmaps compatible with existing digital pathology tools. Code and models are publicly available at https://github.com/AivaraX-AI/MuCTaL.

</details>


### [6] [HECTOR: Hybrid Editable Compositional Object References for Video Generation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08850)
*Guofeng Zhang,Angtian Wang,Jacob Zhiyuan Fang,Liming Jiang,Haotian Yang,Alan Yuille,Chongyang Ma*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: HECTOR is a video generation pipeline that enables fine-grained, compositional control by combining hybrid reference conditioning (images and/or videos) with explicit, user-defined object trajectories, yielding higher visual quality, better reference fidelity, and more controllable motion than prior methods.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Real-world videos contain multiple interacting objects, but most existing generators treat scenes holistically, offering little explicit control over individual elements’ appearance and motion. There is a need for methods that preserve reference fidelity while satisfying complex spatiotemporal constraints and enabling compositional manipulation.

Method: Introduce HECTOR, a generative pipeline that: (1) supports hybrid reference conditioning, simultaneously guided by static images and/or dynamic videos; and (2) lets users explicitly specify each referenced element’s trajectory (location, scale, speed), enforcing precise spatiotemporal behavior while maintaining high-fidelity adherence to the references.

Result: Across extensive experiments, HECTOR outperforms existing approaches in visual quality, preserves references more faithfully, and improves motion controllability.

Conclusion: HECTOR provides practical, fine-grained compositional control for video generation, enabling coherent outputs that meet complex spatiotemporal constraints and adhere closely to visual references, advancing controllable video synthesis.

Abstract: Real-world videos naturally portray complex interactions among distinct physical objects, effectively forming dynamic compositions of visual elements. However, most current video generation models synthesize scenes holistically and therefore lack mechanisms for explicit compositional manipulation. To address this limitation, we propose HECTOR, a generative pipeline that enables fine-grained compositional control. In contrast to prior methods,HECTOR supports hybrid reference conditioning, allowing generation to be simultaneously guided by static images and/or dynamic videos. Moreover, users can explicitly specify the trajectory of each referenced element, precisely controlling its location, scale, and speed (see Figure1). This design allows the model to synthesize coherent videos that satisfy complex spatiotemporal constraints while preserving high-fidelity adherence to references. Extensive experiments demonstrate that HECTOR achieves superior visual quality, stronger reference preservation, and improved motion controllability compared with existing approaches.

</details>


### [7] [Comparative Analysis of Patch Attack on VLM-Based Autonomous Driving Architectures](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08897)
*David Fernandez,Pedram MohajerAnsari,Amir Salarpour,Long Cheng,Abolfazl Razi,Mert D. Pesé*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They benchmark three vision-language driving models under physically realizable adversarial patch attacks in CARLA and find all are highly vulnerable, with multi-frame failures and major drops in critical object detection, revealing architecture-specific weakness patterns.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Vision-language models are entering autonomous driving stacks, but their robustness to real-world (physical) adversarial attacks is unknown; safety-critical deployment demands a fair, systematic robustness assessment across architectures.

Method: Construct a comparative, black-box adversarial evaluation of three VLMs for driving (Dolphins, OmniDrive/Omni-L, LeapVAD). Use physically realizable patch attacks in CARLA. Employ black-box optimization to craft attacks and apply semantic homogenization to ensure fair cross-model comparisons. Measure multi-frame effects and object detection degradation to map vulnerability patterns.

Result: All models exhibit severe vulnerability to physical patch attacks, with sustained failures across frames and substantial degradation of critical object detection; distinct vulnerability profiles emerge per architecture.

Conclusion: Current vision-language designs for autonomous driving lack adequate adversarial robustness and are unsafe without defenses; systematic robustness benchmarks and targeted mitigations are urgently needed before real-world deployment.

Abstract: Vision-language models are emerging for autonomous driving, yet their robustness to physical adversarial attacks remains unexplored. This paper presents a systematic framework for comparative adversarial evaluation across three VLM architectures: Dolphins, OmniDrive (Omni-L), and LeapVAD. Using black-box optimization with semantic homogenization for fair comparison, we evaluate physically realizable patch attacks in CARLA simulation. Results reveal severe vulnerabilities across all architectures, sustained multi-frame failures, and critical object detection degradation. Our analysis exposes distinct architectural vulnerability patterns, demonstrating that current VLM designs inadequately address adversarial threats in safety-critical autonomous driving applications.

</details>


### [8] [Towards Visual Query Segmentation in the Wild](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08898)
*Bing Fan,Minghao Li,Hanzhi Zhang,Shaohua Dong,Naga Prudhvi Mareedu,Weishi Shi,Yunhe Feng,Yan Huang,Heng Fan*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Introduces visual query segmentation (VQS): segment all pixel-level occurrences of a queried object throughout untrimmed videos. Releases VQS-4K (4,111 videos, >1.3M frames, 222 categories) with precise spatio-temporal mask annotations and proposes VQ-SAM, a SAM 2–based multi-stage method with adaptive memory leveraging target and distractor cues, achieving state-of-the-art results on the benchmark.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing visual query localization (VQL) typically finds only the last occurrence and uses coarse bounding boxes, which is insufficient for practical applications that require comprehensive, precise, and temporally complete localization of objects given a visual query.

Method: 1) Build VQS-4K: a large, diverse benchmark pairing each search video with an external query frame and its mask; videos are annotated with spatio-temporal masklets. 2) Propose VQ-SAM: extend SAM 2 with a multi-stage framework that progressively evolves memory across the video using target-specific and background-distractor cues; an Adaptive Memory Generation (AMG) module selects/updates memory entries to guide accurate pixel-level segmentation of all target occurrences.

Result: On VQS-4K, VQ-SAM delivers strong performance and surpasses all existing approaches (significant gains reported in extensive experiments). Dataset, code, and results will be publicly released.

Conclusion: VQS reframes VQL to a more practical, fine-grained task. VQS-4K establishes the first dedicated benchmark, and VQ-SAM serves as a strong baseline that outperforms prior methods, expected to spur further research and real-world applications in video object localization/segmentation.

Abstract: In this paper, we introduce visual query segmentation (VQS), a new paradigm of visual query localization (VQL) that aims to segment all pixel-level occurrences of an object of interest in an untrimmed video, given an external visual query. Compared to existing VQL locating only the last appearance of a target using bounding boxes, VQS enables more comprehensive (i.e., all object occurrences) and precise (i.e., pixel-level masks) localization, making it more practical for real-world scenarios. To foster research on this task, we present VQS-4K, a large-scale benchmark dedicated to VQS. Specifically, VQS-4K contains 4,111 videos with more than 1.3 million frames and covers a diverse set of 222 object categories. Each video is paired with a visual query defined by a frame outside the search video and its target mask, and annotated with spatial-temporal masklets corresponding to the queried target. To ensure high quality, all videos in VQS-4K are manually labeled with meticulous inspection and iterative refinement. To the best of our knowledge, VQS-4K is the first benchmark specifically designed for VQS. Furthermore, to stimulate future research, we present a simple yet effective method, named VQ-SAM, which extends SAM 2 by leveraging target-specific and background distractor cues from the video to progressively evolve the memory through a novel multi-stage framework with an adaptive memory generation (AMG) module for VQS, significantly improving the performance. In our extensive experiments on VQS-4K, VQ-SAM achieves promising results and surpasses all existing approaches, demonstrating its effectiveness. With the proposed VQS-4K and VQ-SAM, we expect to go beyond the current VQL paradigm and inspire more future research and practical applications on VQS. Our benchmark, code, and results will be made publicly available.

</details>


### [9] [Multi-Kernel Gated Decoder Adapters for Robust Multi-Task Thyroid Ultrasound under Cross-Center Shift](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08906)
*Maziar Sabouri,Nourhan Bayasi,Arman Rahmim*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Under cross-center shifts, CNNs better preserve texture for malignancy classification while ViTs better transfer geometric priors for segmentation; adding lightweight decoder-side Multi-Kernel Gated Adapters (MKGA/ResMKGA) mitigates negative transfer and boosts out-of-domain segmentation and CNN-based TI-RADS accuracy.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Multi-task thyroid US systems must jointly segment nodules (geometry/global cues) and assess malignancy (texture/local cues). Domain shifts across centers asymmetrically degrade these cues, and standard shared-backbone designs cause negative transfer between tasks. There is a need to decouple and selectively fuse features to maintain robustness across domains.

Method: (1) Empirically characterize cross-task interference under domain shift using a CNN backbone (ResNet34) and a medical ViT (MedSAM), revealing complementary strengths (ViT for geometry/segmentation, CNN for texture/classification). (2) Propose decoder-side adapters—MKGA and ResMKGA—that refine multi-scale skip features via multi-kernel receptive fields and apply semantic, context-conditioned gating to suppress artifact-prone content before fusion. The adapters are lightweight, plug into multi-task decoders, and aim to preserve task-relevant cues while reducing negative transfer.

Result: Across two thyroid US benchmarks, the adapters increase cross-center robustness: improved out-of-domain segmentation in both backbone families and, notably with CNN backbones, clear gains in TI-RADS diagnostic accuracy compared to standard multi-task baselines.

Conclusion: Decoder-side, gated multi-kernel adapters effectively address asymmetric degradation and negative transfer in multi-task thyroid US under domain shift. Choosing backbones that align with task priors (ViT for geometry, CNN for texture) and adding MKGA/ResMKGA yields more robust segmentation and diagnosis; released code/models will facilitate adoption.

Abstract: Thyroid ultrasound (US) automation couples two competing requirements: global, geometry-driven reasoning for nodule delineation and local, texture-driven reasoning for malignancy risk assessment. Under cross-center domain shift, these cues degrade asymmetrically, yet most multi-task pipelines rely on a single shared backbone, often inducing negative transfer. In this paper, we characterize this interference across CNN (ResNet34) and medical ViT (MedSAM) backbones, and observe a consistent trend: ViTs transfer geometric priors that benefit segmentation, whereas CNNs more reliably preserve texture cues for malignancy discrimination under strong shift and artifacts. Motivated by this failure mode, we propose a lightweight family of decoder-side adapters, the Multi-Kernel Gated Adapter (MKGA) and a residual variant (ResMKGA), which refine multi-scale skip features using complementary receptive fields and apply semantic, context-conditioned gating to suppress artifact-prone content before fusion. Across two US benchmarks, the proposed adapters improve cross-center robustness: they strengthen out-of-domain segmentation and, in the CNN setting, yield clear gains in clinical TI-RADS diagnostic accuracy compared to standard multi-task baselines. Code and models will be released.

</details>


### [10] [Vision-Language Models Encode Clinical Guidelines for Concept-Based Medical Reasoning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08921)
*Mohamed Harmanani,Bining Long,Zhuoxin Guo,Paul F. R. Wilson,Amirhossein Sabour,Minh Nguyen Nhat To,Gabor Fichtinger,Purang Abolmaesumi,Parvin Mousavi*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: MedCBR augments Concept Bottleneck Models with clinical-guideline-grounded text, multimodal contrastive learning, and a reasoning module that produces structured clinical narratives, yielding higher diagnostic AUROCs and improved concept fidelity while enhancing interpretability.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Classic CBMs improve interpretability by predicting human-understandable concepts before the final decision, but they often ignore broader clinical context (guidelines, heuristics), which can reduce reliability in complex medical cases where transparency and guideline conformance matter.

Method: 1) Convert labeled clinical descriptors into guideline-conformant text. 2) Train a concept-based vision-language model with a multitask objective: multimodal contrastive alignment (image–text), supervised concept prediction, and diagnostic classification to jointly ground features, concepts, and pathology. 3) A reasoning model transforms predicted concepts/diagnoses into structured narratives that explain decisions per clinical guidelines.

Result: On medical imaging: AUROC 94.2% (ultrasound) and 84.0% (mammography); improved concept-level performance versus baselines. On non-medical data: 86.1% accuracy, indicating broader applicability.

Conclusion: Embedding clinical guidelines into a concept-based, multimodal pipeline and adding a reasoning stage strengthens both performance and interpretability, offering an end-to-end bridge from image analysis to guideline-aligned clinical explanations. Further clinical validation and robustness checks are needed to ensure reliability across settings.

Abstract: Concept Bottleneck Models (CBMs) are a prominent framework for interpretable AI that map learned visual features to a set of meaningful concepts for task-specific downstream predictions. Their sequential structure enhances transparency by connecting model predictions to the underlying concepts that support them. In medical imaging, where transparency is essential, CBMs offer an appealing foundation for explainable model design. However, discrete concept representations often overlook broader clinical context such as diagnostic guidelines and expert heuristics, reducing reliability in complex cases. We propose MedCBR, a concept-based reasoning framework that integrates clinical guidelines with vision-language and reasoning models. Labeled clinical descriptors are transformed into guideline-conformant text, and a concept-based model is trained with a multitask objective combining multimodal contrastive alignment, concept supervision, and diagnostic classification to jointly ground image features, concepts, and pathology. A reasoning model then converts these predictions into structured clinical narratives that explain the diagnosis, emulating expert reasoning based on established guidelines. MedCBR achieves superior diagnostic and concept-level performance, with AUROCs of 94.2% on ultrasound and 84.0% on mammography. Further experiments on non-medical datasets achieve 86.1% accuracy. Our framework enhances interpretability and forms an end-to-end bridge from medical image analysis to decision-making.

</details>


### [11] [MEGC2026: Micro-Expression Grand Challenge on Visual Question Answering](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08927)
*Xinqi Fan,Jingting Li,John See,Moi Hoon Yap,Su-Jing Wang,Adrian K. Davison*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: MEGC 2026 launches two micro-expression video QA benchmarks—short-video ME-VQA and long-video ME-LVQA—to leverage MLLMs/LVLMs for subtle, temporally aware ME understanding, with evaluation via a public leaderboard.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Micro-expressions are fleeting, low-intensity, and occur under emotional suppression, making them hard to detect and interpret. Recent progress in ME analysis and the rise of powerful multimodal models create an opportunity for standardized, realistic benchmarks that test multimodal reasoning and temporal sensitivity for ME understanding.

Method: Define two tasks: (1) ME-VQA—VQA over short ME video clips to probe recognition, spotting, and understanding using MLLMs/LVLMs; (2) ME-LVQA—VQA over long, realistic videos requiring temporal localization, long-range reasoning, and detection of subtle MEs across extended time. Performance is compared on a public leaderboard.

Result: This is a challenge/benchmark announcement rather than an empirical study: it introduces tasks, data protocols, and an evaluation platform (public leaderboard) to standardize assessment of ME understanding with multimodal models.

Conclusion: By framing ME analysis as VQA at both short and long temporal scales, MEGC 2026 aims to drive advances in multimodal temporal reasoning and subtle ME detection, fostering reproducible progress through open benchmarking and leaderboards.

Abstract: Facial micro-expressions (MEs) are involuntary movements of the face that occur spontaneously when a person experiences an emotion but attempts to suppress or repress the facial expression, typically found in a high-stakes environment. In recent years, substantial advancements have been made in the areas of ME recognition, spotting, and generation. The emergence of multimodal large language models (MLLMs) and large vision-language models (LVLMs) offers promising new avenues for enhancing ME analysis through their powerful multimodal reasoning capabilities. The ME grand challenge (MEGC) 2026 introduces two tasks that reflect these evolving research directions: (1) ME video question answering (ME-VQA), which explores ME understanding through visual question answering on relatively short video sequences, leveraging MLLMs or LVLMs to address diverse question types related to MEs; and (2) ME long-video question answering (ME-LVQA), which extends VQA to long-duration video sequences in realistic settings, requiring models to handle temporal reasoning and subtle micro-expression detection across extended time periods. All participating algorithms are required to submit their results on a public leaderboard. More details are available at https://megc2026.github.io.

</details>


### [12] [TIDE: Text-Informed Dynamic Extrapolation with Step-Aware Temperature Control for Diffusion Transformers](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08928)
*Yihua Liu,Fanjiang Ye,Bowen Lin,Rongyu Fang,Chengming Zhang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: TIDE is a training-free method that enables Diffusion Transformers to generate images at arbitrary higher resolutions and aspect ratios without extra sampling cost by counteracting attention dilution via text anchoring and artifact-aware dynamic temperature control.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: DiT models suffer structural degradation and prompt information loss when extrapolating beyond training resolution due to attention dilution; prior fixes that sharpen attention harm fine-grained semantics and introduce artifacts. A plug-and-play approach that preserves structure and details at higher resolutions is needed.

Method: Analyze DiT’s failure mode and identify an imbalance between text and image tokens as the key source of prompt loss. Propose (1) a text anchoring mechanism to rebalance contributions of text vs. image tokens during generation, and (2) a dynamic temperature control that follows the diffusion process’s spectral progression to suppress artifacts. The approach is training-free, supports arbitrary resolution/aspect ratio, and adds no sampling overhead.

Result: Extensive experiments show improved high-resolution extrapolation quality, better structural fidelity and fine-grained semantics, and fewer artifacts compared with attention-sharpening baselines, while remaining compatible with and easily integrable into SOTA T2I pipelines.

Conclusion: Balancing text-image token influence and adapting temperature across diffusion steps effectively mitigates attention dilution in DiTs, enabling robust, training-free resolution and aspect-ratio extrapolation that maintains detail and reduces artifacts, with broad compatibility for practical deployment.

Abstract: Diffusion Transformer (DiT) faces challenges when generating images with higher resolution compared at training resolution, causing especially structural degradation due to attention dilution. Previous approaches attempt to mitigate this by sharpening attention distributions, but fail to preserve fine-grained semantic details and introduce obvious artifacts. We identify the core factor for prompt information loss, and introduce a text anchoring mechanism to correct the imbalance between text and image tokens. To further eliminate artifacts, we design a dynamic temperature control mechanism that leverages the pattern of spectral progression in the diffusion process. Extensive evaluations demonstrate that TIDE delivers high-quality resolution extrapolation capability and integrates seamlessly with existing state-of-the-art methods.

### [17] [SVG-EAR: Parameter-Free Linear Compensation for Sparse Video Generation via Error-aware Routing](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08982)
*Xuanyi Zhou,Qiuyang Mang,Shuo Yang,Haocheng Xi,Jintao Zhang,Huanzhi Mao,Joseph E. Gonzalez,Kurt Keutzer,Ion Stoica,Alvin Cheung*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: SVG-EAR is a training-free, error-aware sparse attention scheme for video Diffusion Transformers that uses cluster centroids to approximate skipped attention blocks and exactly computes only the highest predicted error blocks, yielding ~1.8–1.9× speedups without degrading fidelity.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Quadratic attention in Diffusion Transformers is a computational bottleneck for video generation. Existing sparsification either drops blocks (information loss) or uses learned predictors (training cost and potential distribution shift). A method is needed to cut attention cost while preserving fidelity, without extra training.

Method: Cluster keys/values within each attention block to exploit their semantic similarity and summarize them with a few centroids. Add a parameter-free linear compensation branch that uses centroids to approximate the contributions of skipped blocks. Use a lightweight probe to estimate per-block compensation error and route exact computation only to blocks with the highest error-to-cost ratios. Provide theory linking attention reconstruction error to clustering quality.

Result: On video diffusion benchmarks with DiTs (Wan2.2 and HunyuanVideo), SVG-EAR improves the quality–efficiency trade-off, forming a better Pareto frontier than prior sparsification. It achieves up to 1.77× and 1.93× speedups while maintaining PSNRs up to 29.759 and 31.043, respectively, and increases throughput at similar generation fidelity.

Conclusion: Training-free centroid compensation plus error-aware routing addresses the main drawbacks of prior sparse attention—avoiding information loss and learned predictors—while preserving fidelity and reducing compute. Effectiveness depends on clustering quality and the probe’s error estimates, but results suggest a practical, drop-in acceleration for video DiTs with theoretical backing.

Abstract: Diffusion Transformers (DiTs) have become a leading backbone for video generation, yet their quadratic attention cost remains a major bottleneck. Sparse attention reduces this cost by computing only a subset of attention blocks. However, prior methods often either drop the remaining blocks, which incurs information loss, or rely on learned predictors to approximate them, introducing training overhead and potential output distribution shifting. In this paper, we show that the missing contributions can be recovered without training: after semantic clustering, keys and values within each block exhibit strong similarity and can be well summarized by a small set of cluster centroids. Based on this observation, we introduce SVG-EAR, a parameter-free linear compensation branch that uses the centroid to approximate skipped blocks and recover their contributions. While centroid compensation is accurate for most blocks, it can fail on a small subset. Standard sparsification typically selects blocks by attention scores, which indicate where the model places its attention mass, but not where the approximation error would be largest. SVG-EAR therefore performs error-aware routing: a lightweight probe estimates the compensation error for each block, and we compute exactly the blocks with the highest error-to-cost ratio while compensating for skipped blocks. We provide theoretical guarantees that relate attention reconstruction error to clustering quality, and empirically show that SVG-EAR improves the quality-efficiency trade-off and increases throughput at the same generation fidelity on video diffusion tasks. Overall, SVG-EAR establishes a clear Pareto frontier over prior approaches, achieving up to 1.77$\times$ and 1.93$\times$ speedups while maintaining PSNRs of up to 29.759 and 31.043 on Wan2.2 and HunyuanVideo, respectively.

### [18] [SkipGS: Post-Densification Backward Skipping for Efficient 3DGS Training](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08997)
*Jingxing Li,Yongjae Leeand,Deliang Fan*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: SkipGS speeds up 3D Gaussian Splatting training by skipping backpropagation on views whose losses have plateaued, yielding ~23% end-to-end speedup without degrading quality.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: In post-densification, backprop dominates runtime while many sampled views provide negligible gradient due to near-plateaued losses. Standard training still backpropagates on every view, wasting compute.

Method: A view-adaptive backward gating scheme: always run the forward pass to maintain per-view loss statistics; compare each sampled view’s current loss to its recent per-view baseline; if consistent (plateau), skip the backward pass; enforce a minimum backward budget to maintain optimization stability. No changes to renderer, representation, or loss, so it’s plug-and-play.

Result: On Mip-NeRF 360, SkipGS cuts post-densification time by 42% and total training time by 23.1%, with comparable reconstruction quality to 3DGS.

Conclusion: Selective backprop based on per-view loss dynamics effectively removes redundant updates in 3DGS, preserves accuracy, and composes with other efficiency strategies for additive gains.

Abstract: 3D Gaussian Splatting (3DGS) achieves real-time novel-view synthesis by optimizing millions of anisotropic Gaussians, yet its training remains expensive, with the backward pass dominating runtime in the post-densification refinement phase. We observe substantial update redundancy in this phase: many sampled views have near-plateaued losses and provide diminishing gradient benefits, but standard training still runs full backpropagation. We propose SkipGS with a novel view-adaptive backward gating mechanism for efficient post-densification training. SkipGS always performs the forward pass to update per-view loss statistics, and selectively skips backward passes when the sampled view's loss is consistent with its recent per-view baseline, while enforcing a minimum backward budget for stable optimization. On Mip-NeRF 360, compared to 3DGS, SkipGS reduces end-to-end training time by 23.1%, driven by a 42.0% reduction in post-densification time, with comparable reconstruction quality. Because it only changes when to backpropagate -- without modifying the renderer, representation, or loss -- SkipGS is plug-and-play and compatible with other complementary efficiency strategies for additive speedups.

### [23] [GST-VLA: Structured Gaussian Spatial Tokens for 3D Depth-Aware Vision-Language-Action Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.09079)
*Md Selim Sarowar,Omer Tariq,Sungho Kim*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: GST-VLA replaces 2D image tokens with a compact 3D Gaussian representation and supervises depth-aware chain-of-thought to yield better grounded spatial reasoning and higher manipulation success on LIBERO and SimplerEnv.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Conventional VLA models operate on 2D patch tokens that lack explicit 3D geometry, hindering precise spatial grounding and action planning. Scalar depth alone misses surface orientation and confidence cues. The goal is to endow VLAs with compact, structured 3D geometry and intermediate spatial reasoning signals to improve precision-critical tasks.

Method: 1) Gaussian Spatial Tokenizer (GST): converts frozen depth and semantic features into 128 anisotropic 3D Gaussian primitives with mean, log-scale covariance (encodes local surface orientation), and opacity (confidence). Spatial attention pooling learns to allocate a fixed token budget to geometrically salient regions. 2) 3D Depth-Aware Chain-of-Thought (DA-CoT): supervises generation of four intermediate spatial thoughts—object grounding, grasp contact geometry, pairwise metric distances, and coarse SE(3) waypoints—while every VLM block cross-attends the raw 256-primitive Gaussian field. 3) A 300M flow-matching action expert with MoE FFNs decodes 7-DoF delta actions via conditional ODE integration, conditioned on VLM states and DA-CoT via dual cross-attention. Training uses a composite loss (L_flow + L_CoT + L_depth) over three progressive stages.

Result: GST-VLA achieves 96.4% on LIBERO (+2.0%) and 80.2% on SimplerEnv (+5.4%). Ablations attribute gains to both GST and DA-CoT, with additive/synergistic effects, especially on precision-demanding tasks.

Conclusion: Explicit 3D Gaussian tokens plus depth-aware chain-of-thought supervision provide stronger spatial grounding and planning, enabling measurable improvements in VLA control. Concentrating the representation on salient geometry and supervising structured spatial intermediates is an effective recipe likely transferable to other embodied AI settings.

Abstract: VLA models encode visual observations as 2D patch tokens with no intrinsic geometric structure. We introduce GST-VLA with two contributions. First, the Gaussian Spatial Tokenizer (GST) converts frozen dense depth and frozen semantic patch features into $N_g{=}128$ anisotropic 3D Gaussian primitives, each parameterized by a metric residual mean $μ\in \mathbb{R}^3$, log-scale covariance $\log σ\in \mathbb{R}^3$, and learned opacity $α\in (0,1)$. The covariance eigenstructure encodes local surface orientation, and opacity provides per-primitive geometric confidence, both inaccessible from scalar depth. Spatial attention pooling with learned queries concentrates the fixed token budget on geometrically salient regions rather than distributing uniformly. Second, 3D Depth-Aware Chain-of-Thought (DA-CoT) reasoning supervises four structured intermediate spatial thoughts, covering 3D object grounding, grasp affordance contact geometry, pairwise metric distances, and coarse SE(3) waypoints, as explicit generation targets in the training loss. A cross-attention sublayer at every VLM transformer block provides direct access to the raw 256-primitive Gaussian field during DA-CoT generation. A 300M-parameter flow-matching action expert with mixture-of-experts feedforward sublayers decodes 7-DoF delta action chunks via conditional ODE integration, conditioned on both VLM hidden states and DA-CoT outputs through dual cross-attention. Trained with composite $\mathcal{L}_\mathrm{flow} + \mathcal{L}_\mathrm{CoT} + \mathcal{L}_\mathrm{depth}$ across three progressive stages, GST-VLA achieves 96.4% on LIBERO (+2.0%), and 80.2% on SimplerEnv (+5.4%). Ablations isolate the contribution of each GST component, each DA-CoT thought, and each training stage, confirming independent and synergistic gains concentrated on precision demanding tasks.

</details>

### [25] [Chain of Event-Centric Causal Thought for Physically Plausible Video Generation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.09094)
*Zixuan Wang,Yixin Hu,Haolan Wang,Feng Chen,Yan Liu,Wen Li,Yinjie Lei*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Treats physically plausible video generation as a causal chain of events. Uses physics-constrained chain-of-thought to decompose prompts into event units and a transition-aware cross-modal prompting pipeline to keep temporal continuity and synthesize keyframes, achieving superior results on PhyGenBench and VideoPhy.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current video diffusion models struggle with commonsense physical reasoning and typically depict only a single moment from a prompt, lacking mechanisms to model deterministic causal progressions. Leveraging LLMs purely for concept injection into prompts is insufficient for temporal causality and continuity. The paper aims to impose physics-grounded causality and temporal structure on generation.

Method: Two modules: (1) Physics-driven Event Chain Reasoning—decomposes a described phenomenon into elementary event units via chain-of-thought, while embedding physical formulas as constraints to reduce causal ambiguity and enforce deterministic dependencies. (2) Transition-aware Cross-modal Prompting (TCP)—maps those event units into temporally aligned vision-language prompts; consolidates discrete event descriptions into a causally consistent narrative and progressively synthesizes/editing visual keyframes for each event to maintain continuity across transitions.

Result: On PhyGenBench and VideoPhy benchmarks, the framework outperforms prior methods in generating physically plausible videos across diverse domains. Specific metrics are not given in the abstract, but the claim is of superior performance and broader generality.

Conclusion: Framing PPVG as a sequence of causally connected events and constraining reasoning with physics formulas, combined with TCP for temporal alignment and progressive keyframe synthesis, improves physical plausibility in video generation. Abstract: Physically Plausible Video Generation (PPVG) has emerged as a promising avenue for modeling real-world physical phenomena. PPVG requires an understanding of commonsense knowledge, which remains a challenge for video diffusion models. Current approaches leverage commonsense reasoning capability of large language models to embed physical concepts into prompts. However, generation models often render physical phenomena as a single moment defined by prompts, due to the lack of conditioning mechanisms for modeling causal progression. In this paper, we view PPVG as generating a sequence of causally connected and dynamically evolving events. To realize this paradigm, we design two key modules: (1) Physics-driven Event Chain Reasoning. This module decomposes the physical phenomena described in prompts into multiple elementary event units, leveraging chain-of-thought reasoning. To mitigate causal ambiguity, we embed physical formulas as constraints to impose deterministic causal dependencies during reasoning. (2) Transition-aware Cross-modal Prompting (TCP). To maintain continuity between events, this module transforms causal event units into temporally aligned vision-language prompts. It summarizes discrete event descriptions to obtain causally consistent narratives, while progressively synthesizing visual keyframes of individual events by interactive editing. Comprehensive experiments on PhyGenBench and VideoPhy benchmarks demonstrate that our framework achieves superior performance in generating physically plausible videos across diverse physical domains. Our code will be released soon.

Method: They propose Knowledge-driven Cognitive Orchestration (MedKCO) that (1) orders pretraining samples via a two-level curriculum using diagnostic sensitivity (importance for diagnosis) and intra-class sample representativeness (prototypicality), and (2) applies a self-paced asymmetric contrastive objective that dynamically adjusts which samples/pairs contribute to learning, accounting for high inter-class similarity in medical images. The approach orchestrates both data scheduling and loss participation during vision–language contrastive pretraining.

Abstract: Medical vision-language pretraining (VLP) models have recently been investigated for their generalization to diverse downstream tasks. However, current medical VLP methods typically force the model to learn simple and complex concepts simultaneously. This anti-cognitive process leads to suboptimal feature representations, especially under distribution shift. To address this limitation, we propose a Knowledge-driven Cognitive Orchestration for Medical VLP (MedKCO) that involves both the ordering of the pretraining data and the learning objective of vision-language contrast. Specifically, we design a two level curriculum by incorporating diagnostic sensitivity and intra-class sample representativeness for the ordering of the pretraining data. Moreover, considering the inter-class similarity of medical images, we introduce a self-paced asymmetric contrastive loss to dynamically adjust the participation of the pretraining objective. We evaluate the proposed pretraining method on three medical imaging scenarios in multiple vision-language downstream tasks, and compare it with several curriculum learning methods. <details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Compositional video generation needs multiple objects with distinct motions, but current methods largely bind high-level semantics to video content without explicitly understanding or controlling different motion categories, causing ambiguity from text prompts and poor disentanglement of motion versus appearance.

Method: Two-stage approach: (1) Planning: parse the prompt into a structured representation of instances and interactions; reason over a motion graph to derive frame-wise shape and position trajectories per instance, disambiguating intended motions. (2) Generation: inject motion cues into a diffusion model via disentangled guidance branches that separately handle motionless regions (appearance stabilization), rigid motion (geometry preservation), and non-rigid motion (local deformation regularization). The modules are model-agnostic and plug into various diffusion architectures.

Result: On real-world benchmarks, the framework shows improved motion synthesis quality and control, with better alignment to specified motion categories and stable appearance across instances. The abstract claims extensive experiments and impressive performance but provides no quantitative details in the excerpt.

Conclusion: Explicit motion factorization combined with pre-generation motion planning improves controllability and fidelity in compositional video generation while remaining compatible with diverse diffusion backbones; code release is forthcoming.

Abstract: Compositional video generation aims to synthesize multiple instances with diverse appearance and motion, which is widely applicable in real-world scenarios. However, current approaches mainly focus on binding semantics, neglecting to understand diverse motion categories specified in prompts. In this paper, we propose a motion factorization framework that decomposes complex motion into three primary categories: motionlessness, rigid motion, and non-rigid motion. Specifically, our framework follows a planning before generation paradigm. (1) During planning, we reason about motion laws on the motion graph to obtain frame-wise changes in the shape and position of each instance. This alleviates semantic ambiguities in the user prompt by organizing it into a structured representation of instances and their interactions. (2) During generation, we modulate the synthesis of distinct motion categories in a disentangled manner. Conditioned on the motion cues, guidance branches stabilize appearance in motionless regions, preserve rigid-body geometry, and regularize local non-rigid deformations. Crucially, our two modules are model-agnostic, which can be seamlessly incorporated into various diffusion model architectures. Extensive experiments demonstrate that our framework achieves impressive performance in motion synthesis on real-world benchmarks. Our code will be released soon.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: Translate report-derived findings into Unified Medical Schema (UMS) JSON field-state pairs using a frozen LLM; apply answerability-aware masking to supervise only verifiable fields; use Structured Prediction Decomposition (SPD) to split cross-attention into orthogonality-regularized query groups that extract complementary visual aspects; pretrain ViTs with this structured supervision and discard the LLM for inference.

Conclusion: Structured, schema-driven supervision from a frozen LLM substantially improves sample efficiency and transfer for medical vision encoders while enabling ViT-only deployment, offering a practical alternative to resource-intensive VLMs in clinical workflows.

Abstract: Vision-language pretraining has driven significant progress in medical image analysis. However, current methods typically supervise visual encoders using one-hot labels or free-form text, neither of which effectively captures the complex semantic relationships among clinical findings. In this study, we introduce VIVID-Med, a novel framework that leverages a frozen large language model (LLM) as a structured semantic teacher to pretrain medical vision transformers (ViTs). VIVID-Med translates clinical findings into verifiable JSON field-state pairs via a Unified Medical Schema (UMS), utilizing answerability-aware masking to focus optimization. It then employs Structured Prediction Decomposition (SPD) to partition cross-attention into orthogonality-regularized query groups, extracting complementary visual aspects. Crucially, the LLM is discarded post-training, yielding a lightweight, deployable ViT-only backbone. We evaluated VIVID-Med across multiple settings: on CheXpert linear probing, it achieves a macro-AUC of 0.8588, outperforming BiomedCLIP by +6.65 points while using 500x less data. It also demonstrates robust zero-shot cross-domain transfer to NIH ChestX-ray14 (0.7225 macro-AUC) and strong cross-modality generalization to CT, achieving 0.8413 AUC on LIDC-IDRI lung nodule classification and 0.9969 macro-AUC on OrganAMNIST 11-organ classification. VIVID-Med offers a highly efficient, scalable alternative to deploying resource-heavy vision-language models in clinical settings.

To this end, we propose PRLF, a Progressive Representation Learning Framework designed for MSA under uncertain missing-modality conditions. PRLF introduces an Adaptive Modality Reliability Estimator (AMRE), which dynamically quantifies the reliability of each modality using recognition confidence and Fisher information to determine the dominant modality.   <summary>Details</summary>

(2) Quality-Aware Prior (QAP) uses a multimodal LLM to generate quality descriptions that condition the diffusion process as an interpretable prior. To address this challenge, we propose a novel super-resolution diffusion model, QUSR, which integrates a Quality-Aware Prior (QAP) with an Uncertainty-Guided Noise Generation (UNG) module. The UNG module adaptively adjusts the noise injection intensity, applying stronger perturbations to high-uncertainty regions (e.g., edges and textures) to reconstruct complex details, while minimizing noise in low-uncertainty regions (e.g., flat areas) to preserve original information. Concurrently, the QAP leverages an advanced Multimodal Large Language Model (MLLM) to generate reliable quality descriptions, providing an effective and interpretable quality prior for the restoration process. ### [35] [RTFDNet: Fusion-Decoupling for Robust RGB-T Segmentation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.09149)
*Kunyu Tan,Mingjian Liang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: RTFDNet is a unified three-branch RGB–Thermal segmentation framework that jointly fuses and decouples modalities to stay robust when one sensor is weak or missing, achieving consistent performance without multi-stage teacher–student training.

  <summary>Details</summary>

A single-stage approach that strengthens unimodal paths while preserving strong fused performance is needed.

Method: A three-branch encoder–decoder: one fused and two unimodal branches. Cross-Modal Decouple Regularization (CMDR) separates modality-specific components from the fused representation and supervises unimodal decoders via stop-gradient targets. However, traditional approaches often overemphasize modality balance, resulting in limited robustness and severe performance degradation when sensor signals are partially missing. Recent advances such as cross-modal knowledge distillation and modality-adaptive fine-tuning attempt to enhance cross-modal interaction, but they typically decouple modality fusion and modality adaptation, requiring multi-stage training with frozen models or teacher-student frameworks. We present RTFDNet, a three-branch encoder-decoder that unifies fusion and decoupling for robust RGB-T segmentation. Synergistic Feature Fusion (SFF) performs channel-wise gated exchange and lightweight spatial attention to inject complementary cues. Cross-Modal Decouple Regularization (CMDR) isolates modality-specific components from the fused representation and supervises unimodal decoders via stop-gradient targets. Region Decouple Regularization (RDR) enforces class-selective prediction consistency in confident regions while blocking gradients to the fusion branch. This feedback loop strengthens unimodal paths without degrading the fused stream, enabling efficient standalone inference at test time. RL could improve this but typically relies on deterministic checkers unavailable for open-ended captioning. The need is for fine-grained, reliable reward signals without hand-crafted or deterministic evaluators.

Method: RubiCap forms a diverse committee of candidate captions per image, has an LLM write a rubric capturing consensus strengths and diagnosing deficiencies of the current policy, converts these into explicit evaluation criteria, and uses an LLM judge to provide structured, multi-dimensional rewards for RL training—replacing single scalar rewards with decomposed assessments. Conclusion: LLM-written rubrics enable effective RL for open-ended dense captioning without deterministic checkers, improving diversity, generalization, and efficiency. Compact models trained with RubiCap can rival or exceed much larger baselines, and their captions enhance downstream VLM pretraining, suggesting a scalable path to high-quality synthetic supervision.

Abstract: Dense image captioning is critical for cross-modal alignment in vision-language pretraining and text-to-image generation, but scaling expert-quality annotations is prohibitively expensive. Reinforcement learning (RL) could overcome these limitations, but its successes have so far been concentrated in verifiable domains that rely on deterministic checkers -- a luxury not available in open-ended captioning. We address this bottleneck with RubiCap, a novel RL framework that derives fine-grained, sample-specific reward signals from LLM-written rubrics. RubiCap first assembles a diverse committee of candidate captions, then employs an LLM rubric writer to extract consensus strengths and diagnose deficiencies in the current policy. These insights are converted into explicit evaluation criteria, enabling an LLM judge to decompose holistic quality assessment and replace coarse scalar rewards with structured, multi-faceted evaluations. Across extensive benchmarks, RubiCap achieves the highest win rates on CapArena, outperforming supervised distillation, prior RL methods, human-expert annotations, and GPT-4V-augmented outputs. On CaptionQA, it demonstrates superior word efficiency: our 7B model matches Qwen2.5-VL-32B-Instruct, and our 3B model surpasses its 7B counterpart. Remarkably, using the compact RubiCap-3B as a captioner produces stronger pretrained VLMs than those trained on captions from proprietary models.

*Mohammed Hassanin,Nour Moustafa,Weijian Deng,Ibrahim Radwan*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: PS-Mamba introduces a topology-aware, hierarchical state-space model for image restoration that preserves local neighborhoods and maintains global coherence via progressive splits and cross-scale shortcuts, achieving linear-time complexity and outperforming recent Mamba- and attention-based baselines on SR, denoising, and JPEG deblocking.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

While SSMs like Mamba scale linearly and capture long-range dependencies, naïve 2D use (flattening) breaks spatial topology and recurrent dynamics cause long-range decay, both harmful for high-fidelity restoration that needs fine local detail and global consistency.

Method: Progressive Split-Mamba (PS-Mamba): (1) geometry-consistent partitioning of feature maps to keep neighborhood integrity before state-space processing; (2) progressive split hierarchy (halves → quadrants → octants) enabling multi-scale modeling with linear complexity; (3) symmetric cross-scale shortcut pathways to pass low-frequency global context between hierarchical levels, mitigating long-range decay and stabilizing information flow.

Result: Across super-resolution, image denoising, and JPEG artifact reduction, PS-Mamba yields consistent and clear-margin improvements versus recent Mamba-based and attention-based models, indicating better trade-offs between locality preservation and global propagation under linear complexity.

Conclusion: A topology-aware hierarchical SSM with cross-scale shortcuts reconciles local structure fidelity and long-range coherence in image restoration. It mitigates the spatial-topology distortion and long-range decay of naïve SSMs, offering an efficient alternative to attention with strong empirical gains across tasks.

Abstract: Image restoration requires simultaneously preserving fine-grained local structures and maintaining long-range spatial coherence. While convolutional networks struggle with limited receptive fields, and Transformers incur quadratic complexity for global attention, recent State Space Models (SSMs), such as Mamba, provide an appealing linear-time alternative for long-range dependency modelling. However, naively extending Mamba to 2D images exposes two intrinsic shortcomings. First, flattening 2D feature maps into 1D sequences disrupts spatial topology, leading to locality distortion that hampers precise structural recovery. Second, the stability-driven recurrent dynamics of SSMs induce long-range decay, progressively attenuating information across distant spatial positions and weakening global consistency. Together, these effects limit the effectiveness of state-space modelling in high-fidelity restoration. We propose Progressive Split-Mamba (PS-Mamba), a topology-aware hierarchical state-space framework designed to reconcile locality preservation with efficient global propagation. Instead of sequentially flattening entire feature maps, PS-Mamba performs geometry-consistent partitioning, maintaining neighbourhood integrity prior to state-space processing. A progressive split hierarchy (halves, quadrants, octants) enables structured multi-scale modelling while retaining linear complexity. To counteract long-range decay, we introduce symmetric cross-scale shortcut pathways that directly transmit low-frequency global context across hierarchical levels, stabilising information flow over large spatial extents. Extensive experiments on super-resolution, denoising, and JPEG artifact reduction show consistent improvements over recent Mamba-based and attention-based models with a clear margin.

### [42] [Distributed Convolutional Neural Networks for Object Recognition](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.09220)
*Liang Sun*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Standard CNNs learn features for all classes and can entangle positive and negative features, making single-class recognition/detection in complex backgrounds heavy and brittle. The authors want a lightweight model that extracts only the target-class features, generalizes well (including to unseen negatives), and simplifies detection in large backgrounds.

Method: Design a loss that maps positive samples to a compact set in a high-dimensional embedding space and maps negatives to the origin. Train a DisCNN so that only positive-class features are retained (nonzero), while negative-class features collapse to zero. This leads to feature disentanglement and a lightweight architecture focused on a few positive features.

Result: Experiments show the learned representations isolate positive-class features from negatives, the model is lightweight, generalizes well on test data, and remains robust when encountering unseen negative classes. Object detection of positives in complex backgrounds becomes straightforward.

Conclusion: By enforcing a clustered-positive/zero-negative embedding via the proposed loss, DisCNN disentangles and compresses target-class features, enabling compact models and simple, robust detection of the positive class even in cluttered scenes.

Abstract: This paper proposes a novel loss function for training a distributed convolutional neural network (DisCNN) to recognize only a specific positive class. By mapping positive samples to a compact set in high-dimensional space and negative samples to Origin, the DisCNN extracts only the features of the positive class. An experiment is given to prove this. Thus, the features of the positive class are disentangled from those of the negative classes. The model has a lightweight architecture because only a few positive-class features need to be extracted. The model demonstrates excellent generalization on the test data and remains effective even for unseen classes. Finally, using DisCNN, object detection of positive samples embedded in a large and complex background is straightforward.

### [44] [HelixTrack: Event-Based Tracking and RPM Estimation of Propeller-like Objects](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.09235)
*Radim Spetlik,Michal Pliska,Vojtěch Vrba,Jiri Matas*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: HelixTrack is a fully event-driven tracker that jointly tracks propeller-like objects and estimates RPM with microsecond latency, enabled by online homography warping to the rotor plane, a Kalman-filtered phase model, and batched pose refinement; it introduces the TQE dataset and outperforms adapted baselines while running faster than real time.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Safety-critical UAV and rotating machinery perception needs microsecond-latency tracking of fast, periodic motion under egomotion and distractors. Conventional frame- and event-based trackers assume smooth motion and fail on periodic signatures like propellers. There is also no public dataset for joint tracking and RPM estimation of such objects.

Method: A fully event-driven pipeline: (1) incoming events are back-warped from the image plane to the rotor plane using an online-estimated homography; (2) a Kalman Filter maintains instantaneous phase estimates for periodic motion; (3) batched iterative updates refine object pose by coupling phase residuals to scene geometry. The system jointly tracks object pose and estimates RPM.

Result: New Timestamped Quadcopter with Egomotion (TQE) dataset: 13 high-resolution event sequences, 52 rotating objects at 2 m and 4 m, increasing egomotion, and microsecond-precision RPM ground truth. HelixTrack processes full-rate events at ~11.8× real time with microsecond latency and consistently outperforms per-event and aggregation-based baselines adapted for RPM estimation.

Conclusion: Modeling periodic motion explicitly in an event-driven framework enables robust, microsecond-latency tracking and RPM estimation of propeller-like objects under egomotion and distractors. HelixTrack is practical for real-time deployment and sets a new benchmark with the TQE dataset, surpassing adapted baselines.

Abstract: Safety-critical perception for unmanned aerial vehicles and rotating machinery requires microsecond-latency tracking of fast, periodic motion under egomotion and strong distractors. Frame-based and event-based trackers drift or break on propellers because periodic signatures violate their smooth-motion assumptions. We tackle this gap with HelixTrack, a fully event-driven method that jointly tracks propeller-like objects and estimates their rotations per minute (RPM). Incoming events are back-warped from the image plane into the rotor plane via a homography estimated on the fly. A Kalman Filter maintains instantaneous estimates of phase. Batched iterative updates refine the object pose by coupling phase residuals to geometry. To our knowledge, no public dataset targets joint tracking and RPM estimation of propeller-like objects. We therefore introduce the Timestamped Quadcopter with Egomotion (TQE) dataset with 13 high-resolution event sequences, containing 52 rotating objects in total, captured at distances of 2 m / 4 m, with increasing egomotion and microsecond RPM ground truth. On TQE, HelixTrack processes full-rate events (approx. 11.8x real time) faster than real time and microsecond latency. It consistently outperforms per-event and aggregation-based baselines adapted for RPM estimation.

First, the Garment Condition Bridge Module (GCBM) builds a garment-cue representation that captures global appearance and semantic identity, enabling robust inference of continuous details under partial visibility. Second, the Flat Structure Constraint Module (FSCM) injects explicit flat-garment structural priors via Flat-Constraint Attention (FC-Attention) at selected denoising stages, improving structural stability beyond text-only conditioning. Extensive experiments on standard VTOFF benchmarks show that BridgeDiff achieves state-of-the-art performance, producing higher-quality flat-garment reconstructions while preserving fine-grained appearance and structural integrity.

Motivation: VFM-based detectors (e.g., CLIP) overfit to strong pretrained semantic priors (identity, content) under distribution shift, ignoring subtle forensic artifacts, which hurts detection on unseen generators and datasets.

To address this issue, we propose \textbf{Geometric Semantic Decoupling (GSD)}, a parameter-free module that explicitly removes semantic components from learned representations by leveraging a frozen VFM as a semantic guide with a trainable VFM as an artifact detector. GSD estimates semantic directions from batch-wise statistics and projects them out via a geometric constraint, forcing the artifact detector to rely on semantic-invariant forensic evidence. Extensive experiments demonstrate that our method consistently outperforms state-of-the-art approaches, achieving 94.4\% video-level AUC (+\textbf{1.2\%}) in cross-dataset evaluation, improving robustness to unseen manipulations (+\textbf{3.0\%} on DF40), and generalizing beyond faces to the detection of synthetic images of general scenes, including UniversalFakeDetect (+\textbf{0.9\%}) and GenImage (+\textbf{1.7\%}).

Considering the box-to-polygon reference shift in Detection Transformers, we propose Polar Deformable Attention and Position-Aware Training Scheme to dynamically update supervision and focus attention on boundary cues. ### [55] [Speeding Up the Learning of 3D Gaussians with Much Shorter Gaussian Lists](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.09277)
*Jiaqi Liu,Zhizhong Han*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They speed up 3D Gaussian Splatting training by making each pixel depend on far fewer Gaussians—via periodically shrinking Gaussian scales, adding an entropy loss to sharpen per-ray alpha weights, and using a progressive resolution schedule—achieving higher efficiency without hurting quality.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 3DGS renders faster and often better than NeRF but training still spends time aggregating many Gaussians per pixel. Reducing the number and influence of Gaussians contributing to each pixel can lower computational cost without degrading fidelity.

Method: 1) Regularly reset/shrink Gaussian scales so each Gaussian covers fewer pixels, shortening per-pixel Gaussian lists. 2) Add an entropy-minimizing constraint on alpha blending weights along each ray, pushing weight distributions to be peakier so only a few Gaussians dominate. 3) Employ a rendering-resolution scheduler that increases resolution progressively to further cut early-stage cost.

Result: On common benchmarks, their approach delivers significant efficiency gains during training while preserving rendering quality compared to state-of-the-art 3DGS variants, according to the abstract.

Conclusion: Targeted sparsification of per-pixel Gaussian contributions—through scale resets, entropy-sharpened blending, and progressive resolution—can accelerate 3DGS training without sacrificing visual quality.

Abstract: 3D Gaussian splatting (3DGS) has become a vital tool for learning a radiance field from multiple posed images. Although 3DGS shows great advantages over NeRF in terms of rendering quality and efficiency, it remains a research challenge to further improve the efficiency of learning 3D Gaussians. To overcome this challenge, we propose novel training strategies and losses to shorten each Gaussian list used to render a pixel, which speeds up the splatting by involving fewer Gaussians along a ray. Specifically, we shrink the size of each Gaussian by resetting their scales regularly, encouraging smaller Gaussians to cover fewer nearby pixels, which shortens the Gaussian lists of pixels. Additionally, we introduce an entropy constraint on the alpha blending procedure to sharpen the weight distribution of Gaussians along each ray, which drives dominant weights larger while making minor weights smaller. As a result, each Gaussian becomes more focused on the pixels where it is dominant, which reduces its impact on nearby pixels, leading to even shorter Gaussian lists. Eventually, we integrate our method into a rendering resolution scheduler which further improves efficiency through progressive resolution increase. We evaluate our method by comparing it with state-of-the-art methods on widely used benchmarks. Our results show significant advantages over others in efficiency without sacrificing rendering quality.

Method: Three key designs: (1) MUSE (Mask Union for Stable Erasure): applies a windowed union during temporal mask downsampling to retain all target regions seen in each window, mitigating missed removals under abrupt motion. (2) DA-Seg (Denoising-Aware Segmentation): a lightweight, decoupled segmentation head with Denoising-Aware AdaLN and training with mask degradation to provide a diffusion-aware localization prior without interfering with content generation. (3) Curriculum Two-Stage Training: Stage I self-supervised pretraining on unpaired real-background videos with online random masks to learn realistic background/temporal priors; Stage II finetuning on synthetic pairs using mask degradation and side-effect-weighted losses to jointly remove objects and associated shadows/reflections and improve cross-domain robustness.
